Older or newer brokers may not support\n    65→ * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n    66→ * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n    67→ * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n    68→ * <p>\n    69→ *\n    70→ * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n    71→ * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n    72→ * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n    73→ * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n    74→ * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n    75→ * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n    76→ * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n    77→ * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n    78→ * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n    79→ * <p>\n    80→ * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n    81→ * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n    82→ * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n    85→ * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n    86→ * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n    87→ * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n    88→ * <p>\n    89→ * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. In this case it will block for up to {@code max.block.ms} milliseconds if \n   841→     * Kafka cluster is unreachable; 2) Allocating a buffer if buffer pool doesn't have any free buffers.\n   842→     * <p>\n   843→     * The result of the send is a {@link RecordMetadata} specifying the partition the record was sent to, the offset\n   844→     * it was assigned and the timestamp of the record. If the producer is configured with acks = 0, the {@link RecordMetadata}\n   845→     * will have offset = -1 because the producer does not wait for the acknowledgement from the broker.\n   846→     * If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#CREATE_TIME CreateTime} is used by the topic, the timestamp\n   847→     * will be the user provided timestamp or the record send time if the user did not specify a timestamp for the\n   848→     * record. If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME LogAppendTime} is used for the\n   849→     * topic, the timestamp will be the Kafka broker local time when the message is appended.\n   850→     * <p>\n   851→     * Since the send call is asynchronous it returns a {@link java.util.concurrent.Future Future} for the\n   852→     * {@link RecordMetadata} that will be assigned to this record. Invoking {@link java.util.concurrent.Future#get()\n   853→     * get()} on this future will block until the associated request completes and then return the metadata for the record\n   854→     * or throw any exception that occurred while sending the record.\n   855→     * <p>\n   856→     * If you want to simulate a simple blocking call you can call the <code>get()</code> method immediately:\n   857→     *\n   858→     * <pre>\n   859→     * {@code\n   860→     * byte[] key = \"key\".getBytes();\n   861→     * byte[] value = \"value\".getBytes();\n   862→     * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\"my-topic\", key, value)\n   863→     * producer.send(record).get();\n   864→     * }</pre>\n   865→     * <p>\n   866→     * Fully non-blocking usage can make use of the {@link Callback} parameter to provide a callback that\n   867→     * will be invoked when the request is complete.\n   868→     *\n   869→     * <pre>\n   870→     * {@code\n   871→     * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\"the-topic\", key, value);\n   872→     * producer.send(myRecord,\n   873→     *               new Callback() {\n   874→     *                   public void onCompletion(RecordMetadata metadata, Exception e) {\n   875→     *                       if(e != null) {\n   876→     *                          e.printStackTrace();\n   877→     *                       } else {\n   878→     *                          System.out.println(\"The offset of the record we just sent is: \" + metadata.offset());\n   879→     *                       }\n   880→     *                   }\n   881→     *               });\n   882→     * }\n   883→     * </pre>\n   884→     *\n   885→     * Callbacks for records being sent to the same partition are guaranteed to execute in order. That is, in the\n   886→     * following example <code>callback1</code> is guaranteed to execute before <code>callback2</code>:\n   887→     *\n   888→     * <pre>\n   889→     * {@code\n   890→     * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key1, value1), callback1);\n   891→     * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key2, value2), callback2);\n   892→     * }\n   893→     * </pre>\n   894→     * <p>\n   895→     * When used as part of a transaction, it is not necessary to define a callback or check the result of the future\n   896→     * in order to detect errors from <code>send</code>. If any of the send calls failed with an irrecoverable error,\n   897→     * the final {@link #commitTransaction()} call will fail and throw the exception from the last failed send. When\n   898→     * this happens, your application should call {@link #abortTransaction()} to reset the state and continue to send\n   899→     * data.\n   900→     * </p>\n   901→     * <p>\n   902→     * Some transactional send errors cannot be resolved with a call to {@link #abortTransaction()}. Takes `MemoryRecords records` (already in RecordBatch format)\n   - Takes `leaderEpoch` to stamp on messages\n   - Delegates to the private `append()` method at line 1030\n\n2. **append() method** at line 1081 (core private append implementation):\n   - **Metadata check** at line 1091: `maybeFlushMetadataFile()` ensures partition metadata is persisted\n   - **Validation** at line 1093: `analyzeAndValidateRecords()` validates records, checks for duplicates\n   - **Trimming invalid bytes** at line 1100: `trimInvalidBytes()` removes any partial/invalid records\n   - **Offset assignment** at lines 1108-1137 (for leader appends):\n     - Uses `LogValidator` to validate and assign offsets to each message\n     - Assigns monotonically increasing offsets starting from `logEndOffset()`\n     - Converts to target compression if needed (line 1112)\n     - Reassigns message format version if needed\n     - Updates `appendInfo` with first/last offset, timestamps\n   - Calls `maybeAddDelayedProduce()` which creates a `DelayedProduce` in the purgatory\n   - The broker waits for follower replicas to acknowledge the append before responding to the producer\n\n2. **Follower Replication Path**:\n   - Followers fetch data from leader via `FetchRequest` (consumer-like behavior)\n   - Followers receive `FetchResponse` with the data from leader\n   - Followers call `UnifiedLog.appendAsFollower()` at line 1053\n   - This bypasses offset assignment (offsets come from leader) and validation, just writes to disk\n   - Followers update their in-sync replica (ISR) status\n\n3. **ISR Management**:\n   - ReplicaManager tracks which followers have caught up\n   - Only when enough replicas have acknowledged (based on `acks` setting) is response sent to producer\n\n## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery\n\n### KafkaConsumer Poll Entry Point\n\nThe consumer calls `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration timeout)` at line 894 (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java:894`):\n\n```java\npublic ConsumerRecords<K, V> poll(final Duration timeout) {\n    return delegate.poll(timeout);\n}\n```\n\nThis delegates to the internal `ConsumerDelegate` which calls the `Fetcher`.\n\n### Fetcher: Building and Sending Fetch Requests\n\nThe `Fetcher` class (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java`):\n\n1. **sendFetches() method** at line 105:\n   - Application calls `commitSync()` (blocking) or `commitAsync()` (non-blocking)\n   - Sends `OffsetCommitRequest` to broker (or group coordinator)\n   - Broker stores offset in `__consumer_offsets` internal topic\n\n2. **Auto Commit** (if enabled):\n   -
